NOTE: note_041

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Therapeutic bronchoscopy — balloon dilation

Patient: [PATIENT], 49-year-old female with post-tracheostomy tracheal stenosis and dyspnea.

Procedure: Bronchoscopy with balloon dilation of tracheal stenosis.
Anesthesia: General anesthesia.
Complications: None.

Findings:
Short segment stenosis at prior tracheostomy site, lumen ~7–8 mm.

Technique:
Flexible bronchoscopy identified stenosis. Balloon dilation performed to 10 mm then 12 mm with improved lumen diameter. Minimal mucosal oozing resolved with suction/cold saline.

Specimens: None.
Plan: PPI and airway humidification; follow-up bronchoscopy in 6–8 weeks.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Patient: [PATIENT], 61-year-old male with dyspnea and moderate left pleural effusion.

Procedure: Ultrasound-guided left thoracentesis.

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Bronchoscopy + EBUS with elastography mention

[PATIENT] is a 70-year-old female with suspected sarcoidosis versus malignancy, with bilateral hilar and mediastinal adenopathy.

Anesthesia: Moderate sedation.
Findings: No endobronchial lesion. EBUS showed enlarged station 7 and 11R; elastography demonstrated relatively stiff pattern in station 7.

Sampling:

7: 6 passes (22G)

11R: 4 passes (22G)

Additional:
Endobronchial biopsies from right mainstem spur x4 for granulomatous evaluation. BAL in right upper lobe.

Specimens: “7 TBNA”, “11R TBNA”, “RMSB endobronchial bx”, “RUL BAL”.
Complications: none.

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Airway stent surveillance and clearance
Patient: [PATIENT], 67-year-old male with prior right mainstem stent for malignant compression.

Procedure: Bronchoscopy with stent toileting and stent repositioning.
Anesthesia: General anesthesia.
Complications: None.

Findings:
Metallic stent in right mainstem bronchus with moderate granulation tissue at proximal edge and inspissated secretions within stent lumen.

Interventions:

Mechanical debridement of granulation tissue using forceps with minimal bleeding.

Cryotherapy applied to focal granulation tissue at proximal stent edge (2 applications).

Stent gently repositioned 5–8 mm distally to optimize proximal edge away from carina.

Airway suctioned clear; distal bronchus patent.

Specimens: None.
Plan: Nebulized saline; airway clearance; follow-up in 3–4 weeks for repeat surveillance bronchoscopy.

NOTE: note_002
================================================================================

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Indication: Hemoptysis and left upper lobe mass on CT in a 58-year-old female.
Procedure: Bronchoscopy, endobronchial biopsy, brushings, BAL, linear EBUS-TBNA.
Sedation: Moderate sedation (midazolam and fentanyl) with topical lidocaine.

Narrative:
Consent obtained and time-out performed. Flexible bronchoscopy was advanced via oral bite block. Vocal cords normal. There was an exophytic lesion at the left upper lobe apicoposterior segment entrance with contact bleeding. Suction and cold saline were used for hemostasis.

Interventions:

Endobronchial biopsies x6 from LUL lesion.

Cytology brush x2 from LUL lesion.

BAL in lingula with 100 mL instilled, 35 mL return, blood-tinged initially then clearing.

EBUS portion:
EBUS scope introduced. Doppler confirmed no intervening vessels. Sampling performed in the following order:

Station 11L: 4 passes (22G)

Station 7: 4 passes (22G)

Station 4L: 3 passes (22G)

Specimens labeled:

“LUL endobronchial bx”

“LUL brush”

“Lingula BAL”

“11L TBNA”

“7 TBNA”

“4L TBNA”

Complications: None. EBL minimal.
Plan: Follow-up pathology; continue hemoptysis precautions; resume diet when awake and safe swallow confirmed.

NOTE: note_006

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
CPT/ICD + HEADINGS TEMPLATE
PRE-DX: Central airway obstruction due to endobronchial tumor (J98.09)
POST-DX: Same
PROCEDURES: Rigid bronchoscopy; mechanical tumor debulking; APC; balloon dilation (codes sometimes: CPT 31641, 31645)
ANESTHESIA: General anesthesia with jet ventilation
EBL: 10 mL
COMPLICATIONS: None

HISTORY/INDICATION:
[PATIENT] is a 69-year-old male with progressive dyspnea and stridor; CT shows distal tracheal narrowing.

PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:
Rigid bronchoscopy performed. Distal trachea demonstrated friable endoluminal tumor causing ~70% obstruction, extending to proximal right mainstem. Mechanical debulking performed using rigid forceps with suction. APC applied to tumor base for hemostasis and devitalization. Balloon dilation performed at distal trachea to 12 mm, then 14 mm with improved lumen caliber. Flexible bronchoscopy through rigid barrel confirmed patency of right and left mainstem bronchi. Residual secretions cleared.

IMPRESSION/PLAN:

Successful debulking with marked improvement in airway diameter.

Admit for observation; humidification and airway clearance.

Follow-up with oncology and pathology from prior biopsy if available; no specimens taken today.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PROCEDURE NOTE — Peripheral bronchoscopy (robotic)

Patient: [PATIENT], 72-year-old male
Indication: Left lower lobe 1.6 cm peripheral nodule with bronchus sign.

Procedures:

Robotic navigation bronchoscopy

Radial EBUS confirmation

Transbronchial biopsy and TBNA
Anesthesia: General anesthesia.
Complications: None.

Description:
Robotic platform docked and registration completed. Navigation to LLL posterior basal target performed. Radial EBUS showed eccentric signal; fluoroscopy used to confirm tool position. TBNA x3 and forceps biopsies x7 obtained. Mild bleeding controlled with wedge positioning and cold saline.

Specimens: “LLL TBNA”, “LLL bx”.
Plan: CXR in PACU; follow pathology.

NOTE: note_001
================================================================================

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS: Mediastinal adenopathy; pulmonary nodule (R91.1, R59.0)
POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS: Same
PROCEDURES: Bronchoscopy with BAL; Linear EBUS-TBNA of mediastinal/hilar lymph nodes (include codes: CPT 31624, 31652)
ANESTHESIA: General anesthesia with LMA
ESTIMATED BLOOD LOSS: Minimal
COMPLICATIONS: None

INDICATION: [PATIENT] is a 64-year-old male with right upper lobe pulmonary nodule and PET-avid mediastinal nodes for diagnosis and staging.

FINDINGS:

Trachea and main carina normal.

Mild bronchitic secretions in right lower lobe; no endobronchial mass.

EBUS: Enlarged station 4R and station 7 with heterogeneous echotexture; station 11L small but visualized.

PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:
After informed consent and time-out, flexible bronchoscopy was performed through the LMA. Airway inspection was completed to segmental level bilaterally. BAL was performed in the right upper lobe posterior segment with 120 mL instilled, 48 mL returned, mildly turbid. The EBUS bronchoscope was then introduced. Doppler was used prior to each pass.

EBUS-TBNA sampling:

Station 4R: 5 passes with 22G needle

Station 7: 6 passes with 22G needle

Station 11L: 3 passes with 22G needle

SPECIMENS:

“4R TBNA” (passes 1–5)

“7 TBNA” (passes 1–6)

“11L TBNA” (passes 1–3)

“RUL BAL”

IMPRESSION/PLAN:

No endobronchial lesion.

Await cytology/pathology and flow as ordered.

CXR in PACU if clinically indicated; routine recovery and follow-up with referring team.

PROCEDURE NOTE (COMPLEX)
Patient: [PATIENT], 71-year-old male
Indication: Right lower lobe peripheral nodule 1.9 cm with intermediate PET uptake; staging requested.
Post-procedure diagnosis: Same.

Procedures performed:

Robotic navigational bronchoscopy to right lower lobe target

Radial EBUS confirmation

Transbronchial needle aspiration, transbronchial biopsy, cryobiopsy (peripheral)

BAL (right lower lobe)

Linear EBUS-TBNA of station 7 and station 11R

Anesthesia: General anesthesia with ETT.
Fluoroscopy: Used.
Complications: None.
EBL: Minimal.

Technique:
After consent and time-out, robotic platform was docked. Registration completed to pre-procedure CT. Navigation was performed to the RLL superior segment target. Radial EBUS demonstrated an eccentric signal with adjacent vessel excluded by Doppler. Tool position was confirmed with fluoroscopy.

Sampling at RLL target:

TBNA: 3 passes (19G)

Transbronchial biopsy: 6 forceps biopsies

Cryobiopsy: 2 samples (1.1 mm probe), thaw and retrieval without significant bleeding
Hemostasis achieved with wedge positioning and cold saline. BAL performed in RLL with 120 mL instilled, 52 mL return.

Staging:
Linear EBUS performed next.

Station 7: 4 passes (22G)

Station 11R: 3 passes (22G)

Specimens:
A) “RLL target TBNA”
B) “RLL forceps bx”
C) “RLL cryobiopsy”
D) “RLL BAL”
E) “7 TBNA”
F) “11R TBNA”

Plan:
Routine recovery; post-procedure CXR in PACU; follow-up pathology and cytology; resume anticoagulation per referring team when appropriate.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Pleuroscopy with biopsy ± talc pleurodesis (narrative)

Patient: [PATIENT], 72-year-old female with recurrent right pleural effusion and pleural nodularity on CT.

Procedure: Medical pleuroscopy with pleural biopsies and talc pleurodesis.
Anesthesia: Monitored anesthesia care.
Complications: None.

Technique/Findings:
After ultrasound localization, single port entry into right pleural space. Approximately 900 mL serosanguinous fluid aspirated. A chest tube was placed and connected to suction.

Specimens:
“Right pleural biopsy” (multiple)

Plan:
Chest tube management per protocol; pain control; follow pathology and cytology.

THERAPEUTIC BRONCHOSCOPY — COMBINED
PRE: Subglottic/tracheal stenosis
POST: Improved airway caliber

Procedure(s): Flexible bronchoscopy; balloon dilation; electrocautery radial incisions.
Anesthesia: General anesthesia.
EBL: Minimal.

Findings:
Short-segment tracheal stenosis ~1.5 cm length, lumen ~8 mm.

Interventions:

Specimens: None.
Plan: Steroid taper per protocol; PPI; follow-up bronchoscopy in 6–8 weeks.

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Airway stent repositioning + balloon dilation

Patient: [PATIENT], 63-year-old male with metallic stent in left mainstem for malignant compression.

Procedure: Bronchoscopy with balloon dilation and stent repositioning.
Anesthesia: General anesthesia.
Complications: None.

Findings:
Proximal stent edge abutting carina with granulation tissue and partial obstruction.

Interventions:
Balloon dilation performed within stent to 10 mm then 12 mm. Stent gently repositioned distally ~1 cm to optimize carinal clearance. Granulation tissue suctioned and lightly debrided.

Specimens: None.
Plan: Nebulized saline; airway clearance; follow-up surveillance bronchoscopy in 3–4 weeks.

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Peripheral bronchoscopy — cryobiopsy included

Patient: [PATIENT], 56-year-old female
Indication: Diffuse peripheral nodularity and suspected organizing pneumonia; need tissue.

Procedure: Navigation bronchoscopy to right lower lobe target; transbronchial cryobiopsy x3; BAL.
Anesthesia: General anesthesia.
Complications: None.

Technique:
Navigation to RLL lateral basal region. Radial EBUS showed eccentric signal. Cryobiopsy performed with 1.1 mm probe x3 with brief freeze cycles, retrieved without significant bleeding. Hemostasis with wedging and cold saline. BAL performed in RLL (150 mL in, 62 mL out).

Specimens: “RLL cryobiopsy”, “RLL BAL”.
Plan: CXR in PACU; monitor for delayed bleeding; follow pathology/cultures.

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Flexible bronchoscopy with therapeutic aspiration and BAL

[NAME:REDACTED] is a 46-year-old female with fever and new diffuse infiltrates, concern for infection in an immunocompromised host.

Sedation: Moderate sedation.
Findings: Thick purulent secretions in bilateral lower lobes, no focal endobronchial lesion.

Procedure: Bronchoscopy via oral approach. Airway cleared with suctioning and saline lavage. BAL performed in right middle lobe with 100 mL instilled, 40 mL return, cloudy. Additional washings obtained from left lower lobe basilar segments.

Specimens: “RML BAL”, “LLL washings”.
Complications: none. EBL none.

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
THERAPEUTIC BRONCHOSCOPY — OBSTRUCTION
Indication: Malignant left mainstem bronchus narrowing with post-obstructive pneumonia in a 72-year-old male.

Procedure: Rigid bronchoscopy with mechanical debulking and balloon dilation.
Anesthesia: General anesthesia with jet ventilation.
Findings: Near-occlusive tumor at proximal left mainstem, thick purulent secretions distal.

Interventions:
Mechanical debulking performed until lumen ~70% restored. Balloon dilation to 10 mm then 12 mm. Distal secretions suctioned and cleared. Airway patency confirmed to lobar bronchi.

Specimens: None today.
EBL: 15 mL.
Complications: None.
Plan: Admit/observe; antibiotics per primary team; consider stent if recurrent obstruction.

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Bronchoscopy + EBUS staging (minimal headings)

A 73-year-old male with newly diagnosed right upper lobe carcinoma was brought for mediastinal staging. Under general anesthesia, bronchoscopy demonstrated normal tracheobronchial anatomy without endobronchial tumor. Linear EBUS identified station 4R (12 mm) and station 7 (15 mm). Doppler negative. TBNA performed:

4R: 5 passes (22G)

7: 5 passes (22G)

10R: 3 passes (22G)

Specimens labeled by station. EBL minimal. No complications. Plan for routine recovery and follow-up pathology.

NOTE: note_007

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
OP NOTE — Airway stent
Patient: [PATIENT], 62-year-old female
Indication: Post-intubation tracheal stenosis with recurrent dyspnea.

Procedure: Bronchoscopy with balloon dilation and silicone tracheal stent placement.
Anesthesia: General anesthesia.
Complications: None.

Findings:

Circumferential stenosis 2.5 cm below vocal cords, lumen ~6–7 mm.

Distal trachea and bronchi otherwise patent.

Technique:
After consent/time-out, flexible bronchoscopy identified the stenotic segment. Balloon dilation performed sequentially to 10 mm then 12 mm. A silicone tracheal stent was deployed across the stenosis (straight silicone stent, 14 mm x 40 mm). Position confirmed bronchoscopically with proximal edge below cords and distal edge above carina. Minimal mucosal oozing treated with suction and cold saline.

Plan:

Nebulized saline and airway clearance regimen.

Follow-up bronchoscopy in 4–6 weeks for stent surveillance or sooner for symptoms.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Navigational bronchoscopy + EBUS staging combined (Template E style, no explicit codes)

Patient: [PATIENT], 63-year-old female
Indication: RUL 2.3 cm spiculated nodule; staging requested.

Anesthesia: General anesthesia with ETT.
Procedures:

Navigation bronchoscopy to RUL target with radial EBUS confirmation

Sampling of RUL target with TBNA and biopsies

Linear EBUS-TBNA of mediastinal/hilar nodes

Procedure:
Flexible bronchoscopy showed no endobronchial lesion. Navigation performed to RUL posterior segment lesion. Radial EBUS showed concentric signal. TBNA x3 and forceps biopsies x8 obtained; minimal bleeding controlled with wedging.

Linear EBUS staging followed:

4R: 3 passes (22G)

7: 4 passes (22G)

11R: 3 passes (22G)

“RUL TBNA”

“RUL bx”

“4R TBNA”

“7 TBNA”

“11R TBNA”

Complications: None. EBL minimal.
Plan: Post-procedure CXR; follow pathology and cytology; outpatient follow-up with pulmonary and oncology.

NOTE: note_021

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Airway stent removal
Patient: [PATIENT], 61-year-old female with benign left mainstem stenosis previously treated with stent, now improved.

Procedure: Bronchoscopy with silicone stent removal.
Anesthesia: General anesthesia.
Complications: None.

Details:
Flexible bronchoscopy demonstrated silicone stent in left mainstem bronchus with minimal granulation tissue. Rigid forceps used to grasp stent retrieval loop and stent removed en bloc without mucosal injury. Post-removal inspection showed mild residual stenosis with lumen ~11–12 mm and good distal airway patency. Minor oozing resolved with suction.

Specimens: None.
Plan: Observe for bronchospasm; airway clearance; follow-up in clinic with repeat imaging as indicated.

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Indication: Pleural effusion, diagnostic and therapeutic drainage.
Patient: [PATIENT], 55-year-old male with dyspnea and large right pleural effusion on ultrasound.

Procedure: Ultrasound-guided right thoracentesis.
Anesthesia: Local lidocaine.
Estimated volume removed: 1100 mL.
Complications: None.

Details:
Bedside ultrasound confirmed a large anechoic effusion with atelectatic lung, safe window in posterior axillary line. After sterile prep/drape and local anesthesia, a catheter-over-needle system was advanced into pleural space with free-flowing straw-colored fluid. 1100 mL removed with symptom improvement. Procedure terminated due to patient cough and near-complete drainage.

Specimens:

“Pleural fluid” sent for cell count/diff, protein, LDH, pH, glucose, Gram stain/culture, cytology.

Plan:
Post-procedure CXR per protocol; monitor for chest pain and dyspnea; follow-up results with primary team.

Procedure note: Bronchoscopy, BAL, transbronchial biopsy
Patient: [PATIENT], 52-year-old female with new bilateral ground-glass opacities and hypoxemia.

NOTE TEXT:

Narrative op note — minimal headings

Indication: Persistent right lower lobe consolidation in a 47-year-old female, rule out infection.
Procedure: Flexible bronchoscopy with BAL and bronchial washings.
Sedation: Moderate sedation with topical lidocaine.

Technique/Findings:
Time-out completed. Scope advanced orally. Airways notable for erythematous mucosa and copious purulent secretions from right lower lobe basilar segments. No mass or active bleeding seen.

Interventions:

Therapeutic aspiration with saline aliquots.

BAL in right lower lobe lateral basal segment (120 mL instilled, 44 mL return).

Additional bronchial washings from right lower lobe.

Specimens:
“RLL BAL”, “RLL washings”

Complications: None.
Plan: Follow cultures; continue pulmonary hygiene.

Peripheral bronchoscopy (cone-beam confirmation) + BAL

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Peripheral bronchoscopy (cone-beam CT assisted)

Patient: [PATIENT], 66-year-old male
Indication: RML 1.4 cm nodule, high suspicion; need diagnosis.

Procedure: Computer-assisted navigation bronchoscopy; radial EBUS; transbronchial biopsy; bronchial brushing.
Anesthesia: General anesthesia.
Imaging: Cone-beam CT used for confirmation.
Complications: None.

Narrative:
Navigation performed to RML medial segment. Radial EBUS showed concentric signal. Cone-beam CT confirmed tool within lesion. Sampling included TBNA x2, forceps biopsies x8, and brush x1. Hemostasis achieved with wedging. No pneumothorax noted on end-procedure imaging.

Specimens: “RML bx”, “RML brush”, “RML TBNA”.
Plan: CXR in PACU; follow pathology.

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
THERAPEUTIC BRONCHOSCOPY — AIRWAY OBSTRUCTION

PRE: Central airway obstruction due to tumor (J98.09)
POST: Improved airway patency
Procedure: Rigid bronchoscopy; mechanical debulking; APC
Anesthesia: General anesthesia with jet ventilation
EBL: 20 mL
Complications: None

Indication:
[PATIENT] is a 66-year-old male with severe dyspnea and right mainstem obstruction on imaging.

Findings/Interventions:
Rigid bronchoscopy demonstrated friable endoluminal tumor in right mainstem with ~80% obstruction. Mechanical debulking performed, followed by APC for hemostasis. Flexible bronchoscopy confirmed right upper lobe bronchus patent and right lower lobe segments patent. Residual secretions cleared.

Specimens: None today.
Plan: Admit for airway observation; humidification and airway clearance; coordinate oncology.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Airway stent placement — silicone Y stent

Patient: [PATIENT], 70-year-old female
Indication: Malignant distal tracheal and main carina narrowing.

Procedure: Rigid bronchoscopy with silicone Y stent placement.
Anesthesia: General anesthesia with jet ventilation.
Complications: None.

Findings:
Extrinsic compression at distal trachea and carina with dynamic collapse.

Technique:
Rigid bronchoscopy performed. Airway calibrated and secretions cleared. Silicone Y stent deployed with tracheal limb positioned above carina and bronchial limbs into right and left mainstem bronchi. Final position confirmed with flexible bronchoscopy through the rigid barrel. Airway patency markedly improved.

Stent: Silicone Y stent, 15 x 12 x 12 mm (tracheal x RMB x LMB), length per standard sizing.
Specimens: None.
Plan: Nebulized saline, airway clearance regimen, follow-up bronchoscopy for surveillance.

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Airway stent surveillance + granulation management

Patient: [PATIENT], 58-year-old male with prior tracheal stent for benign stenosis.

Procedure: Bronchoscopy with stent toileting and granulation tissue treatment.
Anesthesia: General anesthesia.
Complications: None.

Findings:
Silicone tracheal stent in place with moderate granulation tissue at distal edge and adherent secretions.

Interventions:

Mechanical debridement of granulation tissue with forceps.

APC applied to focal granulation areas for hemostasis.

Stent lumen suctioned clear.

Specimens: None.
Plan: Nebulized saline; consider inhaled steroid per protocol; follow-up bronchoscopy in 4–6 weeks.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Robotic navigational bronchoscopy + fiducial placement

Patient: [PATIENT], 74-year-old male
Indication: Left lower lobe posterior basal nodule planned for SBRT; need tissue diagnosis and fiducial placement.

Procedures:

Robotic navigation to LLL target

Radial EBUS confirmation

Transbronchial biopsy and TBNA

Fiducial marker placement x3
Sedation: General anesthesia.
Complications: None.

Technique:
Navigation completed to target in LLL posterior basal segment. Radial EBUS demonstrated eccentric signal; fluoroscopy used to confirm tool position. TBNA x3 and forceps biopsies x7 obtained. Three fiducials deployed around lesion margins under fluoroscopy with stable position at completion. Minimal bleeding.

Specimens: “LLL TBNA”, “LLL bx”.
Plan: Post-procedure CXR; coordinate with radiation oncology; follow pathology.
